````text
  &lt;head&gt;
		&lt;style&gt;
			p {padding:0px; margin:0px;}
		&lt;/style&gt;
	&lt;/head&gt;
  &lt;body&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
Explanation of Recovered Elements validation errors:
    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;ul&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
&lt;b&gt;REF&lt;/b&gt;&amp;#160;error: The element is a Recovered Element. This element are referenced by other element in the project. These element are also listed by other error - SRE or URE respectively.
      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
&lt;b&gt;SRE&lt;/b&gt; error: The element which now became recovered is displayed in a diagram. Diagrams may have more than one symbol of recovered element. Each symbol of Recovered Element will be listed as SRE error. An example of this error is the recovered element &amp;quot;List&amp;quot; is represented in diagram.
      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
&lt;b&gt;URE&lt;/b&gt; error: The element has a meta-property reference to a recovered element. An example of this error is an attribute &amp;quot;Collection&amp;quot; is of type &amp;quot;List&amp;quot; which is now became a recovered element.

      &lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;/ul&gt;
  &lt;/body&gt;
&lt;/html&gt;
</text>
	</mdElement>
	<mdElement elementClass='TextBox' xmi:id='_17_0_4_9020291_1378294837597_750317_4726'>
		<properties>
			<mdElement elementClass='BooleanProperty'>
				<propertyID>HTML_TEXT</propertyID>
				<propertyDescriptionID>HTML_TEXT_DESCRIPTION</propertyDescriptionID>
				<value xmi:value='true'/>

		</properties>
		<geometry>49, 917, 868, 329</geometry>
		<mdOwnedViews/>
		<text>&lt;html&gt;
  &lt;head&gt;
		&lt;style&gt;
			p {padding:0px; margin:0px;}
		&lt;/style&gt;
	&lt;/head&gt;
  &lt;body&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
Recovered elements indicate that there are unresolved references in your project.

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
&amp;#160;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
An unresolved reference means that your project contains an element that continues referring to some used project element, which became inaccessible, because, for example, the element is no longer shared, the element was removed or moved to a non-shared location, and so on.

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
&amp;#160;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
To maintain your model integrity and project composition, when element is inaccessible, MagicDraw recovers the inaccessible elements. This allows for maintaining in your project references that are indicated as unresolved.

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
&amp;#160;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
It is highly recommended to eliminate recovered elements from your model. This can be done in one of the following ways:

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
&amp;#160;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;ul&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
By eliminating the reasons of the element recovery. This is the case when recovered elements still exist. Find the reason of the element recovery and eliminate it, for example, share the package that contains the recovered element, move back the element from a non-shared location to the shared one, and so on.

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
By restoring recovered elements. This is the case when recovered elements no longer exist, but can be restored from the bits of information MagicDraw still has. The restored element will have only ID, name, and type.

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
By managing the unresolved references that refer to the appropriate recovered elements. This is the case, when recovered elements no longer exist and cannot be restored.

      &lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/body&gt;
&lt;/html&gt;</text>
	</mdElement>
	<mdElement elementClass='TextBox' xmi:id='_17_0_4_9020291_1378295031212_670372_4739'>

  &lt;body&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
To learn how to avoid triggering element recovery in your project, read the following recommendations:

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;ol&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
Avoid unexpected modifications of shared elements (for example, removing a shared element or moving the element to a non-shared location, etc.).

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
Configure MagicDraw so that it prompts your confirmation to proceed a potentially dangerous action (for example, attempting to stop sharing a package, removing the content of a shared package, or moving elements from one used project to another, when both projects are used in the read-write mode).

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
Select the relevant level of model integrity and project composition inspection.

      &lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;/body&gt;
&lt;/html&gt;</text>
````

````text
<?xml version='1.0' encoding='UTF-8'?>

<mdOwnedViews>
	<mdElement elementClass='TextBox' xmi:id='_11_5EAPbeta_f720368_1150786673917_658721_974'>
		<properties>
			<mdElement elementClass='BooleanProperty'>
				<propertyID>HTML_TEXT</propertyID>
				<propertyDescriptionID>HTML_TEXT_DESCRIPTION</propertyDescriptionID>
				<value xmi:value='true'/>

		<geometry>35, 98, 674, 290</geometry>
		<mdOwnedViews/>
		<text>&lt;html&gt;
  &lt;head&gt;
		&lt;style&gt;
			p {padding:0px; margin:0px;}
		&lt;/style&gt;
	&lt;/head&gt;
  &lt;body&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
This sample describes &lt;b&gt;model decomposition&lt;/b&gt; functionality introduced in MagicDraw v11.5. Two new features were added:      
&lt;br&gt;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;ul&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Editable (read-write) project usages&lt;/b&gt;. This feature allows editing used project contents in-place, as if they were in the main project. &amp;quot;Code Level&amp;quot; project is mounted as read-write and illustrates this feature.

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Unloadable/notloadable project usages&lt;/b&gt;. This feature is useful in many ways. The main use case is on-demand used projects loading (used projects are kept not loaded to save resources and are only loaded when necessary). The purpose of this is to improve performance when working with large projects, having multiple used projects. Also if unloaded used projects have indexes, their contents are visible and they can be used without ever loading them. It also allows working on part of the large project without having all the used projects files (perhaps you took part of the project for home work).

      &lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;/ul&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
      
&lt;br&gt;This sample is derived from the Magic Library sample, with the different emphasis. Magic Library sample demonstrates modeling techniques and this sample concentrates on model decomposition techniques.

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
&amp;#160;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
All the used project settings, demonstrated in this sample, can be seen in the &lt;b&gt;Used Project Options&lt;/b&gt; dialog (&lt;b&gt;Options-&amp;gt;Project Usages&lt;/b&gt; command from main menu). There is a viewlet, explaining this sample at &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nomagic.com/files/viewlets/MD_viewlets_Model_Decomposition.html?ml=1&quot;&gt;No Magic site&lt;/a&gt;.      
&lt;br&gt;

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;

			</mdElement>

			</mdElement>
````

````text
		<geometry>35, 378, 560, 245</geometry>
		<compartment compartmentID='TAGGED_VALUES2'/>
		<mdOwnedViews/>
		<text>&lt;html&gt;
  &lt;head&gt;
		&lt;style&gt;
			p {padding:0px; margin:0px;}
		&lt;/style&gt;
	&lt;/head&gt;
  &lt;body&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
This was the class, which was previously (during the last save) accessible in the used project [domain.mdzip]. Now (during opening of the project) the class is not accessible in the project.

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
Reasons why the element became not accessible in the project might be:

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;ul&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
The element was removed from that used project;

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
The element was moved to another project, which is not used in the main project

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
The element was moved to a not-shared place of the same project

      &lt;/li&gt;
      &lt;li&gt;
Users stopped sharing elements of the project, which caused this element to become not accessible.

      &lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;/ul&gt;
    &lt;p&gt;
In this sample case, the class was removed, and two separate classes were introduced - ArrayList and LinkedList.

    &lt;/p&gt;

    &lt;p&gt;
As a subsequence, the old class &amp;quot;List&amp;quot; is displayed as &amp;quot;Recovered Element&amp;quot; (There is a R character adornment at the top left), because the main project still maintain references to this element, and allows to solve all invalid references even the target element became not accessible.

    &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;/body&gt;
&lt;/html&gt;</text>
````
